  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_611fc3fc-6eb9-4016-88af-e207602f41af'

<span id="freeTextContainer4997673193908843517">Will she accept his offer before the clock strikes midnight?<br/><br/>Sophie Beckett never dreamed she'd be able to sneak into Lady Bridgerton's famed masquerade ball—or that "Prince Charming" would be waiting there for her! Though the daughter of an earl, Sophie has been relegated to the role of servant by her disdainful stepmother. But now, spinning in the strong arms of the debon</span>
  <span id="freeText4997673193908843517" style="display:none">Will she accept his offer before the clock strikes midnight?<br /><br />Sophie Beckett never dreamed she'd be able to sneak into Lady Bridgerton's famed masquerade ball—or that "Prince Charming" would be waiting there for her! Though the daughter of an earl, Sophie has been relegated to the role of servant by her disdainful stepmother. But now, spinning in the strong arms of the debonair and devastatingly handsome Benedict Bridgerton, she feels like royalty. Alas, she knows all enchantments must end when the clock strikes midnight.<br /><br /><i>Who was that extraordinary woman?</i> Ever since that magical night, a radiant vision in silver has blinded Benedict to the attractions of any other—except, perhaps this alluring and oddly familiar beauty dressed in housemaid's garb whom he feels compelled to rescue from a most disagreeable situation. He has sworn to find and wed his mystery miss, but this breathtaking maid makes him weak with wanting her. Yet, if he offers his heart, will Benedict sacrifice his only chance for a fairy tale love?<br /><br /><i>Alternate cover for ISBN 0380815583 / 9780380815586</i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13572720656680663707"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg' width='200' height='150' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b><i>*Unpopular opinion ahead!!!*</i> </b> <br/><br/>I have one thing to say: <b>SCREW YOU, BENEDICT BRIDGERTON!</b> <br/><br/>I'll be the first to admit that I was really, really enjoying this story at the start. I mean, I adore <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/474459.Rosalyn_Landor' title='Rosalyn Landor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rosalyn Landor</a>, who is a narrating queen, and I like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn' title='Julia Quinn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Julia Quinn</a>, who is very consistent for me. However, as I moved further and further along in the story, I realized that <b>I wanted to punch Benedict in the face... hard.</b><br/><br/><b>Benedict treats Sophie like utter trash. </b>He blackmails her to either become his mistress </span>
  <span id="freeText13572720656680663707" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b><i>*Unpopular opinion ahead!!!*</i> </b> <br><br>I have one thing to say: <b>SCREW YOU, BENEDICT BRIDGERTON!</b> <br><br>I'll be the first to admit that I was really, really enjoying this story at the start. I mean, I adore <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/474459.Rosalyn_Landor" title="Rosalyn Landor" rel="nofollow noopener">Rosalyn Landor</a>, who is a narrating queen, and I like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn" title="Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Quinn</a>, who is very consistent for me. However, as I moved further and further along in the story, I realized that <b>I wanted to punch Benedict in the face... hard.</b><br><br><b>Benedict treats Sophie like utter trash. </b>He blackmails her to either become his mistress or move into his family's house as a servant because he won't even entertain the idea of marrying someone as lowly as her, and then has the audacity to be insulted when she isn't genuflecting in gratitude. <br><br><b>He tells her that if she doesn't tell him to stop WELL before they have sex, he won't be able to stop... because, apparently, he is an <i>asshole</i>.</b> Well, that makes a VIRGIN feel safe and loved. <br><br>He sexually harasses her, ignores her pleas to be left alone, and then is acts like a spoiled baby when he finds out her true identity. HE IS TRASH. The only person who I liked was Benedict's mom, who at least finds some courage to do something and think outside the box. <br><br><b>I'm still angry about this book, even after I finished it.</b> Traaaaaaaaaaash!<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time" rel="nofollow noopener">goodreads</a>|<a href="https://www.instagram.com/heatherk_dentistinmysparetime/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a>|<a href="https://twitter.com/DentistHeatherK" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>|<a href="http://www.myfictionnook.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a></span>

<div id="review_2624799594" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2624799594" />
    <a title="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession"><img alt="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511556834p2/28967089.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2624799594?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession" href="/user/show/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession">Jessica&#39;s Totally Over The Top Book Obsession</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=liked-audiobook-version">liked-audiobook-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=reread-worthy">reread-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28967089-jessica-s-totally-over-the-top-book-obsession?shelf=listened-to-on-audio">listened-to-on-audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2624799594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14112051668537693082"><b>4.5 Love at first sight Stars</b><br/><br/><a href='https://imgur.com/6T0Us3G' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545275141ra/26774500.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Going into An offer from a Gentleman I was a bit worried. I had a friend tell me that Benedict (the hero) ask Sophie (the heroine) to be his mistress over and over for most of the book. That he went on about how she wasn't of his class. She had told me it ruined the read for her. I hate that mistress bullshit in books. It's one of the reasons I avoided most historical romance novels for years. I hate cheating! A mistress is just a side chick, that wasn't good eno</span>
  <span id="freeText14112051668537693082" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Love at first sight Stars</b><br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/6T0Us3G" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545275141ra/26774500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Going into An offer from a Gentleman I was a bit worried. I had a friend tell me that Benedict (the hero) ask Sophie (the heroine) to be his mistress over and over for most of the book. That he went on about how she wasn't of his class. She had told me it ruined the read for her. I hate that mistress bullshit in books. It's one of the reasons I avoided most historical romance novels for years. I hate cheating! A mistress is just a side chick, that wasn't good enough to marry. That shit bothers me. It's just so disrespectful to women. Yes I know that was how things were back then but it still pisses me off. However I was enjoying this series so much that I figured I would just have to take one for the team. Read it and get it over with I don't have to love it just read it and then I could go to the next book. Shockingly I really ended up loving this book. <br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/I32197D" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545275141ra/26774499.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book reads as a cute retelling of Cinderella, with poor Sophie being the mistreated bastard daughter of an earl. Julia Quinn did a great job of making Sophie's step-mother Araminta a total evil bitch. I hated her so much and I felt she didn't get her comeuppance. I really wanted her to pay for the things she did to Sophie and her own daughter Posy. I thought Sophie was a wonderful heroine. She was sweet, resilient, a bit sassy, and smart. I love that she had such dignity. I was a little worried I would dislike Benedict, but I really loved him too. I did get a tad upset that he kept asking her to be his mistress, but not like I thought I would. I felt he loved her and treated her well. With that and the way things were way back when, and the fact that he realized he was wrong for asking that of her and apologized. I found myself forgiving Benedict right along with Sophie. <br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/gwq1X1F" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545275141ra/26774498.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I thought Benedict and Sophie were a cute together. I loved that their relationship was built up so well. That fact is most likely what made it easier to forgive Benedict for the whole "be my mistress" crap. On top of loving Sophie and Benedict, I adore the Bridgertons. The whole family is just so easy to love. I also really liked Sophie's step-sister Posy. I was glad that in the end she wasn't overlook and forced to deal with the evil that was her mother. This retelling of Cinderella was cute and flowed well. I had to stop once to feed my family and I found myself thinking about the book the whole time. I couldn't wait to get back to it and see what happened next. That is the mark of a great book. I can't wait to read Colin's book. On a side note, I listened to this book on Audio and Rosalyn Landor did an amazing job of bringing this story to life. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14112051668537693082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1198670194" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1198670194" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198670194?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198670194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13383964923818847688"><b>Hi, my name is Katerina and I am addicted to Bridgertons.</b><br/><br/>I've been dreaming of balls, banquets and gowns since I was a little girl, historical romance is my sanctuary from the small and big disappointments of daily life <i>(i.e. work - read - sleep - repeat)</i>, and during 2018 I've written more 3star reviews than my entire life.<br/>I would appreciate some help.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498103962ra/23092683.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Thank you.<br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“In her heart she longed for this man, dreamed of a life that could never be.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Now, before I start rambling on the wonderful</span>
  <span id="freeText13383964923818847688" style="display:none"><b>Hi, my name is Katerina and I am addicted to Bridgertons.</b><br><br>I've been dreaming of balls, banquets and gowns since I was a little girl, historical romance is my sanctuary from the small and big disappointments of daily life <i>(i.e. work - read - sleep - repeat)</i>, and during 2018 I've written more 3star reviews than my entire life.<br>I would appreciate some help.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498103962ra/23092683.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thank you.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“In her heart she longed for this man, dreamed of a life that could never be.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Now, before I start rambling on the wonderful moments I expecienced when I followed Sophie and Benedict's journey, I need to state that those three starts you see above do not mean I didn't enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9408584.An_Offer_From_a_Gentleman__Bridgertons___3_" title="An Offer From a Gentleman (Bridgertons, #3) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">An Offer From a Gentleman</a>, because I did. The imprint of my butt on my living room's couch can attest to that. It's just that I enjoyed <i>more</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/110391.The_Duke_and_I__Bridgertons___1_" title="The Duke and I (Bridgertons, #1) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Duke and I</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/861326.The_Viscount_Who_Loved_Me__Bridgertons___2_" title="The Viscount Who Loved Me (Bridgertons, #2) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Viscount Who Loved Me</a> <i>(which is my favorite so far)</i>, and I have to be fair and rank them accordingly. Putting that aside, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9408584.An_Offer_From_a_Gentleman__Bridgertons___3_" title="An Offer From a Gentleman (Bridgertons, #3) by Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">An Offer From a Gentleman</a> was a tad different from its predecessors. It was <b>a Cinderella retelling</b>, infused with <b>sizzling tension</b>, a generous dose of <b>angst</b> and <b>drama</b>, and the <b>trademark Bridgerton humor</b> and impossible situations that can warm even the coldest heart. Sophie is the illegitimate daughter of an earl, relegated to a servant by her cruel stepmother further to her father's death. But Fate smiles on her when (with a little help) she manages to attend the Bridgerton masquerade ball and meets the Second Son, Benedict, who is immediately besotted by the mysterious young woman with the silver dress. For one night, Sophie feels happy. Wanted. Belonging. But when the clock strikes midnight, the bubble bursts and she returns to her hard life, which is about to get harder. Two years pass by. Benedict has not forgotten that woman, but when he meets an intriguing servant that sees straight through his soul, he is torn and confused: should he move on, or wait for the mysterious woman to reappear and find his happily ever after with her? Little does he know that Sophie Beckett is both women.<br><br>When you dive in the third instalment of the Bridgerton series, you don't attend many social events. You don't lose yourself waltzing or avoiding Ambitious Mamas <i>(or going after eligible bachelors, depending on the side of this deadly race)</i>. On the contrary, you sew and clean and dream of a better life next to a girl who has never experienced love or affection, who cannot forget even for a single moment that she was born out of wedlock and spent half her life serving the people who were supposed to be her family. Sophie is a <b>resilient</b> character, true to her ideals, determined to never repeat her mother's mistakes and sentence her children to the contempt and disapproval of the society she faced all those years. But how is it possible to preserve her dignity and her morals when her Prince Charming, the man that haunts her dreams, reddens her cheeks and makes her crave things no proper maiden should offers her a life without struggles and destitution, in exchange for her beliefs and the vow to herself? Benedict Bridgerton wants Sophie with a burning passion. But she's a simple maid, he cannot possibly marry her, so he asks her to become his mistress. And that's what left a bitter taste in my mouth. Not the proposal, per se, but his <b>insistence</b> and <b>self-absorption</b>. Benedict was a caring, sweet yet sarcastic character who at times was very endearing, but these two traits, and the refusal to understand Sophie's motives, were the reason I <i>(occasionally)</i> wanted to smack his beautiful head.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480609738ra/21330451.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sophie, on the other hand, she was admirable and strong, but her tendency to keep secrets perplexed the situation and caused <i>(unnecessary)</i> drama and heartbreak. However, I <b>felt</b> this story to my very bones. I <b>ached</b>, <b>laughed</b> <i>(especially when the wonderfully loud Bridgerton family made an appearance)</i>, <b>swooned</b> and <b>sighed</b>, and that's what makes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/63898.Julia_Quinn" title="Julia Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Quinn</a>, and the historical romance genre <i>(please remind me to write a review for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/114162.Secrets_of_a_Summer_Night__Wallflowers___1_" title="Secrets of a Summer Night (Wallflowers, #1) by Lisa Kleypas" rel="nofollow noopener">Secrets of a Summer Night</a> sometime this year)</i> ideal when I am in the mood for <b>not particularly complicated, yet heartwarming and delicious romance with a touch of fairydust</b>, which, to be honest, happens a lot lately.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506311920ra/24005087.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, since I may or may not have ordered the next two books, like another Lady Whistledown, <b>I'll keep you posted on the whereabouts of the Bridgerton family this summer.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13383964923818847688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chan ☆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chan ☆" href="/user/show/48727754-chan">chan ☆</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48727754-chan?shelf=2020">2020</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3599158156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10562845180192008280"><b>perfectly fine</b><br/><br/>which sounds boring, and in truth this book kind of was as well. not boring in the sense that the story was overly dull or drawn out, but in the way that your average run of the mill historical can be. <br/><br/>this book was based on Cinderella and while i initially loathed the idea, it turned out to be a fun retelling. i think the main reason that this story isn't more than 3 star for me though is the lack of relationship development. we get a lot of sophie in her own head and a lot of her</span>
  <span id="freeText10562845180192008280" style="display:none"><b>perfectly fine</b><br /><br />which sounds boring, and in truth this book kind of was as well. not boring in the sense that the story was overly dull or drawn out, but in the way that your average run of the mill historical can be. <br /><br />this book was based on Cinderella and while i initially loathed the idea, it turned out to be a fun retelling. i think the main reason that this story isn't more than 3 star for me though is the lack of relationship development. we get a lot of sophie in her own head and a lot of her poor treatment by her stepmom in the start of the story. but i didn't really see why the hero and heroine liked each other beyond the heroine taking a polite interest in the hero's "hidden depths." there just weren't enough moments beyond him trying to convince her to be his mistress that really established a foundation for the relationship.<br /><br />overall, this was perfectly enjoyable but definitely not memorable. i'm just reading through these at this point in preparation for the netflix adaptation.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9288326657295958463">Excellent! Excellent! <b>Excellent!</b> This is a fantastic read! Quinn’s best so far for me. She has an amazing way to draw you into the story from the first few pages and you’re smiling from the get-go right up to the end :) She even manages to take you on a sudden heart-breaking emotional roller coaster ride that really gives you the chills and makes you want to cry for the h/h as a couple. This contrasts so well with the rest of the light-hearted story making the situation all the more poignant. <br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText9288326657295958463" style="display:none">Excellent! Excellent! <b>Excellent!</b> This is a fantastic read! Quinn’s best so far for me. She has an amazing way to draw you into the story from the first few pages and you’re smiling from the get-go right up to the end :) She even manages to take you on a sudden heart-breaking emotional roller coaster ride that really gives you the chills and makes you want to cry for the h/h as a couple. This contrasts so well with the rest of the light-hearted story making the situation all the more poignant. <br /><br />The heroine Sophie is great and Benedict, who you never really hear from at the start of the series, is an incredibly loving hero. Makes you just sigh every time he says and does something –oh ya and then there’s his tenacity! He wants her and he’ll do whatever it takes to have her. He says to her quietly at one point:<br /><br /><i>“I can live with you hating me …. I just can’t live without you.”</i> <br /><br />Kill me why don’t you 8) You can literally feel his frustration breaking his soul when she rejects him time and again.<br /><br />There’s this one steamy scene that will leave you panting when all is said and done! Big woo hoo there :D<br /><br />Quinn’s story is exactly how I’d picture a regency romance to be. There’s a secret, a fab couple, believable problems, strong main characters as well as secondary characters, great sexual tension, brilliant writing and all set against a wonderful regency backdrop. This is the kind of novel you wish wouldn’t end, <u>BUT</u> there’s another book so the series continues! <br /></span>

For me, this is the epitome of everything I love about romance and happily ever after. <br /><br />There’s a charming, yet flawed hero, a sweet heroine with profound inner strength and resolve who overcomes all odds, powerful emotional conflict, realistic drama, lush sensuality, intense passion, and witty humor.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300549247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13723071026143013189">Absolutely flawless! It is one of my favorites of the series, also got a place of my <i>all-time favorites</i> shelf!<br/><br/>It is a Cinderella story with charming characters, perfect plot and character delineation, twists and turns, adorable and moving romantic scenes, sweet and funny moments.<br/><br/>Although it is based on a fairy tale, the emotions and relationships are presented in a realistic way.<br/><br/>I love Benedict, he is my favorite Bridgerton! He is persevering, sincere, and very romantic. I love his humor, his st</span>
  <span id="freeText13723071026143013189" style="display:none">Absolutely flawless! It is one of my favorites of the series, also got a place of my <i>all-time favorites</i> shelf!<br /><br />It is a Cinderella story with charming characters, perfect plot and character delineation, twists and turns, adorable and moving romantic scenes, sweet and funny moments.<br /><br />Although it is based on a fairy tale, the emotions and relationships are presented in a realistic way.<br /><br />I love Benedict, he is my favorite Bridgerton! He is persevering, sincere, and very romantic. I love his humor, his struggling between two women who actually are the same.<br /><br />I also sympathize with Sophie, her hard life and situation. She is strong and sweet, and true to her principles. I didn’t agree with her last decision, when she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[left the Bridgerton house <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but the final scene makes up for it - it is amazing beyond expectations. Araminta’s evil character is well-done. I admire Lady Bridgerton, and hope to see Posy again. Brilliant ending!<br /><br /><i>An Offer From a Gentleman</i> is a perfect romance!<br /><br /><br /><a href="http://exinasreadings.tumblr.com/tagged/An-Offer-from-a-Gentleman" rel="nofollow noopener">My favorite quotes.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13723071026143013189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2552257832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2552257832" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2552257832?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2552257832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15619160848878606575"><em>This is third in the Bridgertons series. Couples from the first two show up and some events are referenced and there are definite winks at those who have read the others. In all, I recommend reading these in order.</em><br/><br/>Normally, I'd snark about skipping this one because it sucks, but I'm a definite outlier in that opinion. Most of my GR friends rated this very high so you might want to take this review with a grain of salt. Or more. I'll admit that I'm relieved that my problem isn't related to the Ci</span>
  <span id="freeText15619160848878606575" style="display:none"><em>This is third in the Bridgertons series. Couples from the first two show up and some events are referenced and there are definite winks at those who have read the others. In all, I recommend reading these in order.</em><br /><br />Normally, I'd snark about skipping this one because it sucks, but I'm a definite outlier in that opinion. Most of my GR friends rated this very high so you might want to take this review with a grain of salt. Or more. I'll admit that I'm relieved that my problem isn't related to the Cinderella pattern overlaying the story. I expected that to warp the story more than it did but it was relatively benign, all told.<br /><br />Like Cinderella, Sophie's defining characteristic is being a victim. Her life sucks and that's largely due to having suck parents. Her step-mother is a complete monster but her father wasn't a gem, either. The story breaks from the Cinderella mold about there. There's a costume ball where she loses an article of clothing that gives a clue to her identity and then we're done with the fairy tale. Benedict doesn't use it to track her down, her situation changes and Quinn pretty much forges her own story from there. This is not a bad thing, except that I had hoped for a bit more cheerful good will and kindness and that's not Sophie. She feels every bit of the injustice done her. She's not a complainer or anything, but man her life sucked and being cheerful in the face of that would have been expecting a bit much.<br /><br />Benedict, on the other hand, is not a prince, is not charming, and spends most of the story bullying Sophie to get what he wants. He has a single act of humanity (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[saving her from being raped <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>), but that's not so much to his credit as it is kind of the baseline of what I'd expect from a human being witnessing her plight. And it's all downhill from there. He has zero compassion and less empathy and is forever thundering around manipulating and whining to get his own way. I kept waiting for a light to go off in his head for every new thing he learns about Sophie's life so far. In vain, it turns out.<br /><br />Exacerbating this empathy hole is the power differential between the two characters. It'd be one thing if he were being all demandy of someone who could reasonably stand up to him, but Sophie doesn't have that power. She has literally nobody in her corner and yet he feels perfectly justified forcing her to his will, up to and including threatening to turn her in for theft if she doesn't comply. A theft, by the way, that he'd be making up. So it's not enough to threaten to leave her in the middle of nowhere with no money or even spare clothing. No, he has to threaten being transported to some hideous place like Australia. Frankly, I'm thinking she'd get the better end of the deal if she had made him carry through. There's got to be someone non-horrible in Australia and heaven knows that she has nothing keeping her in England.<br /><br />I finished the last half of this in a kind of hate-fueled fugue. I should have dnf'd. I knew I should have. But I kept going. I do like the Bridgerton family and Violet (the mom) continues to shine, here. Her empathy and support and love was the one bright light in this otherwise blighted story.<br /><br /><strong>A note about Steamy</strong>: There's a single explicit sex scene and a couple that were nearly there. So this is light on my steam tolerance. I kind of hated every intimate advance, however, because Benedict is such a complete snotrag. How can she even stand being around the man, let alone kissing him? Ugh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15619160848878606575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1847524173" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1847524173" />
    <a title="KatieV" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18620847-katiev"><img alt="KatieV" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390618322p2/18620847.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1847524173?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KatieV" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KatieV" href="/user/show/18620847-katiev">KatieV</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1847524173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10483797266902069230">Solid 4 stars. My favorite of the series (from what I've read).<br/><br/>Again, I listened to the excellent narration by Rosalyn Landor. No complaints there.<br/><br/>**** SPOILERS ****<br/><br/>This was definitely a Cinderella story. A nod is even given to the slippers Sophie wore to the ball, but with a twist. There was enough angst here to take the story out of Disney territory and into the realm of an adult fairy tale.<br/><br/>Sophie was the unacknowledged daughter of an Earl. The product of his dalliance with a house maid who di</span>
  <span id="freeText10483797266902069230" style="display:none">Solid 4 stars. My favorite of the series (from what I've read).<br /><br />Again, I listened to the excellent narration by Rosalyn Landor. No complaints there.<br /><br />**** SPOILERS ****<br /><br />This was definitely a Cinderella story. A nod is even given to the slippers Sophie wore to the ball, but with a twist. There was enough angst here to take the story out of Disney territory and into the realm of an adult fairy tale.<br /><br />Sophie was the unacknowledged daughter of an Earl. The product of his dalliance with a house maid who died in childbirth. The Earl provided her a home at his country estate and told the world she was his ward. He never acted as a father and paid her little attention, but she was cared for and educated like a female of his class. Her true identity was an open secret, as she looked very much like her father and his family.<br /><br />After the Earl dies unexpectedly, Sophie is left to the mercy of her evil stepmother and stepsisters (one of the two sisters isn't evil, but she's afraid to stand up to her mom and sister). Provisions had been made in the will for Sophie to have a home until she was 20 and to provide her a dowry, but the stepmom didn't tell her about the dowry. She spent the dowry and turned Sophie into an unpaid servant.<br /><br />The housekeeper who helped raise Sophie plays the part of the fairy godmother and sends her off to the Bridgerton masquerade ball wearing one of her deceased grandmother's dresses and the Countess' shoes. She meets the Bridgerton's second son, Benedict, and it's love at first sight for both. Of course, she must disappear at midnight...<br /><br />Sophie was kicked out of her home after the ball when the countess discovered she attended (those damn shoes!). She'd have likely just been nastier and worked Sophie harder, but she was furious when Benedict came to the home to "meet her daughters" in an effort to ferret out his mystery woman Sophie had left a glove behind that was monogrammed with her dead grandmother's initials, giving him a clue to her origin. The Countess was not amused that the much coveted Mr. Bridgerton was truly interested in her hated slave/unacknowledged stepdaughter. Benedict leaves their home puzzled and none the wiser and continues to search for his mystery love.<br /><br />Several years pass before the two meet again. Sophie had since been working as a ladies maid in several different households. Benedict saves her from being attacked by the son of her employer and his drunken friends and takes her to his country home with a promise of getting her employment with his mother. He's attracted to her, but doesn't recognize her because she'd been masked at the ball. He finds something familiar but can't quite put the puzzle together. Sophie lies when asked if they'd ever met. She never wanted him to know because she realized their difference in station would prevent a marriage and make her simply mistress material.<br /><br />Benedict saw her as mistress material anyway and engages in some underhanded ploys to keep her in his clutches. He doesn't force her by any means, but does blackmail her to ensure she works in his mother's household instead of disappearing as she wanted to do. He hoped to keep her around so he could work on convincing her to be his mistress, something she refused to do even after giving in and giving him her virginity. Sophie was determined not to follow in her mother's footsteps and have a bastard child that may suffer the way she had suffered. Benedict's assurances that any children of hers would be cherished by him did not convince her. She knew he'd eventually have to marry and, from bitter experience, did not trust what would happen to her children if he died young like her father had.<br /><br />I thought the differences in station and social mores of the day that made Sophie a suitable mistress, but not wife, made the story more interesting. The modern woman in me wanted to shake Benedict at times for being so arrogant and condescending, but that was fitting for the times. Sophie didn't expect marriage, but most readers will be of a totally different mindset. It made for some great angst.<br /><br />Of course, this is a romance and we get the big reveal, which exposed Sophie as the mystery lady from the ball and revealed to the world that she was actually a gently raised "ward" of the dead earl who'd had her dowry stolen by the evil countess and not a servant. Predictably, Benedict had decided to damn society and forget his beloved "mystery woman" to marry Sophie anyway - right before the big reveal. That satisfies the romantic ideals, despite being unrealistic for the times. I knew it would all turn out to be a perfect HEA, but there was enough angst around the subject to satisfy me - especially given the fact that this was a "fluffy" Julia Quinn romance and not meant to be historically accurate.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10483797266902069230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_252576555" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/252576555" />
    <a title="Erika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6721219-erika"><img alt="Erika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511329430p2/6721219.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252576555?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erika" href="/user/show/6721219-erika">Erika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6523483-an-offer-from-a-gentleman">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fairy tale romance readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6721219-erika?shelf=auto-buy-author">auto-buy-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6721219-erika?shelf=best-of-heroes">best-of-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6721219-erika?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6721219-erika?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6721219-erika?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6721219-erika?shelf=ladies-of-quality">ladies-of-quality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6721219-erika?shelf=fairy-tales-retelling">fairy-tales-retelling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252576555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15303637599183258011">Stepback cover<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380365809i/717955.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"I can live with you hating me," he said to the closed door. "I just can't live without you"</i>
</blockquote><br/><i>The Duke and I</i> gave us a sweet romance, <i>The Viscount Who Loved Me</i> gave us a hilarious one, and <i>An Offer From a Gentleman</i> gave us a magical one.<br/><br/>This third book of the series is about love at the first sight that strike you like a thunderbolt and haunt you for the rest of your life. It happens to Benedict Bridgerton when he sees the beauty in silver gown with radiant smile at the Bridgerto</span>
  <span id="freeText15303637599183258011" style="display:none">Stepback cover<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380365809i/717955.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I can live with you hating me," he said to the closed door. "I just can't live without you"</i>
</blockquote><br><i>The Duke and I</i> gave us a sweet romance, <i>The Viscount Who Loved Me</i> gave us a hilarious one, and <i>An Offer From a Gentleman</i> gave us a magical one.<br><br>This third book of the series is about love at the first sight that strike you like a thunderbolt and haunt you for the rest of your life. It happens to Benedict Bridgerton when he sees the beauty in silver gown with radiant smile at the Bridgerton's masquerade ball party. He doesn't know who she is, except that she's the only guest in the party who doesn't know his identity (even with mask everyone still able to recognized the Bridgertons). She also doesn't know how to dance. But it feels like magic when he talks to her, when he teach her how to dance, when he kiss her.. and then it's midnight and she's already gone. <br><br>Sophie runs when the clock strikes midnight. She's back to reality as a nobleman's bastard daughter and also a maid. She knew the entire evening has been a lie. But she'll always remember the tall and handsome gentleman who has made her feel like a princess. Her charming prince is out of reach. She might not see him again but she'll always has her memory.<br><br>So I thought I knew what would likely to happen next. She left her shoe, he would have search for her and finally find her with a stepmother and two stepsisters. The shoe fits for her only and they will live HEA.<br>I was wrong.<br>Benedict search for her, but he couldn't find her. <br><br>Benedict loves the mysterious woman, but he doesn't even know her. Then Sophie walks into his life as a maid and their romance stands up in the middle of passion, secrets, and memories. It broke my heart to see Benedict's struggling with his own feeling, torns between what he feels for Sophie and the mysterious lady without knowing he's falling in love with the same woman twice. <br><br>And poor Sophie. She loves Benedict but she realizes he can't marry her. The last thing she wants is to become mistress and has child born in shame, just like her.<br><br>The road to HEA was not easy at all for them. There's Benedict's love to the mysterious woman which he must let go, Sophie's secrets to be revealed, and most important of all is their love is forbidden. This book gave us a piece of truth about what could have happened at the time if two people from different social classes fall in love. They couldn't marry and everything would still be alright. There are consequences they must accept and sacrifices they must make. <br><br>I adored this love story, truly a beautiful one. A fairytale with some pieces of reality. Very touching but still have some humors. What I loved most with the Bridgertons series is that it was not just about love and passion, but also about love and family. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Look up," he ordered gently.<br>"But I'll stumble."<br>"You won't," he promised. "I won't let you. Look into my eyes."<br>Sophie did as he asked, and the moment her eyes touched his, something inside her seemed to lock into place, and she could not look away. He twirled her in circles and spirals around the terrace, slowly at first, then picking up speed, until she was breathless and giddy.<br>And all the while, her eyes remained locked on his.<br>"What do you feel?" he asked.<br>"Everything!" she said, laughing.<br>"What do you hear?"<br>"The music." Her eyes widened with excitement. "I hear the music as I've never heard it before."<br>His hands tightened, and the space between them diminished by several inches. "What do you see?" he asked.<br>Sophie stumbled, but she never took her eyes off his. "My soul," she whispered. "I see my very soul."</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15303637599183258011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780380815586" href="/book/show/110385.An_Offer_From_a_Gentleman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3209146-sam-s2-im-made-of-awesomness?shelf=bridgerton-series">bridgerton-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3209146-sam-s2-im-made-of-awesomness?shelf=next-in-the-series">next-in-the-series</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135760236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1196345036823897730">Whenever reading a Julia Quinn novel, it's always an all nighter for me! Forget the family, forget dinner? The only thing that would get my eyes unglued from the pages, would be a life and death emergency.<br/><br/> An Offer from a Gentleman has characters that are full of spunk and fire. This was the perfect Cinderella story that is tried and true. Except in this Cinderella story she is able to keep her wits about herself and remain practical except when both our hero and Cinderella come in contact with </span>
  <span id="freeText1196345036823897730" style="display:none">Whenever reading a Julia Quinn novel, it's always an all nighter for me! Forget the family, forget dinner? The only thing that would get my eyes unglued from the pages, would be a life and death emergency.<br /><br /> An Offer from a Gentleman has characters that are full of spunk and fire. This was the perfect Cinderella story that is tried and true. Except in this Cinderella story she is able to keep her wits about herself and remain practical except when both our hero and Cinderella come in contact with one another. It offers an interesting twist on the original love story in which there is always a twist.<br /><br />Benedict and Sophia are both such lovable characters. I loved the plot and was cheering when her Sophia’s stepmother got her comeuppance. Sophie and Benedict were both seeking the loves they felt was unattainable. This novel was fun, adventurous and absolutely heart-racing.<br /><br />Ms. Quinn really paid attention to every small detail and while reading I feel myself being taken to another time and place and I would hate to be the family member to disturb such a time. There was great attention to the characters self worth. I loved how tough Sophie was and how smart she was and at the same time show how utterly naughty Benedict was.<br /><br />In summary this story was a great fairytale.<br /></span>

<div id="review_258623683" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258623683" />
    <a title="Nadine Jones" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/115626-nadine-jones"><img alt="Nadine Jones" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1180985415p2/115626.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258623683?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadine Jones" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadine Jones" href="/user/show/115626-nadine-jones">Nadine Jones</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780380815586" href="/book/show/110385.An_Offer_From_a_Gentleman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115626-nadine-jones?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115626-nadine-jones?shelf=era-regency">era-regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258623683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6224558676855142865">I like Julia Quinn, I really do, but this was not her finest moment. Looking back on "Bridgertons" #1 & #2, maybe this just is not her finest series. This book was so ... blah. And the hero was such an ASS. On the plus side, it was nice that the heroine was not from conventional society, she is the bastard daughter of an earl, raised as his ward until his death, at which point she is Cinderella to the evil stepmother and two step-sisters. (She even secretly goes to a ball, meets the hero, and th</span>
  <span id="freeText6224558676855142865" style="display:none">I like Julia Quinn, I really do, but this was not her finest moment. Looking back on "Bridgertons" #1 &amp; #2, maybe this just is not her finest series. This book was so ... blah. And the hero was such an ASS. On the plus side, it was nice that the heroine was not from conventional society, she is the bastard daughter of an earl, raised as his ward until his death, at which point she is Cinderella to the evil stepmother and two step-sisters. (She even secretly goes to a ball, meets the hero, and then flees at midnight. I really liked the fairytale aspect and had high hopes for the book at that point. That was before I knew the hero was going to turn out to be an ass.)<br /><br />The hero is the second Bridgerton son, Benedict. The heroine is Sophia (Sophie) Beckett. They meet, they fall in love, she flees, they don't see each other for years, she finds work as a housemaid, he saves her from rape and catches cold while rescuing her, she nurses him back to health in a little "cottage" he happens to own (yeah, got the hurt-comfort going both ways there), he teases her mercilessly, she falls in love with him all over again. Well, so far so good - it's a little tedious, a little blah, but not SO bad. They start making out on the forest floor, and this is where is all goes wrong. Our Sophie, being a bastard child herself, has vowed to never ever have sex out of wedlock, since she cannot bring her own horrid fate on her child. So, while she really REALLY wants to schtup our hero, she says no. He invites her to be his mistress, and want for nothing. She turns him down. He continues to push the issue. This is where he becomes an ass. (SPOILER AHEAD) It'll come as no surprise to hear that he does eventually talk her into have sex with him (ASS) and she regrets the action, although she loves him and it was a moment to treasure, blah blah blah ... He CONTINUES to insist that she become his mistress, even after she has quite CLEARLY told him no, and even told him WHY. He says "well surely you can't expect me to marry you!" ASS. <br /><br />More events unfold until the inevitable denouement, which I'm sure you can guess, though I will not reveal all (for those few who may be surprised). By this time I was so completely disgusted with him that I couldn't possibly be happy for them.<br /><br />Hmm I was going to give this 2 stars, but I just got so worked up writing this review, remembering how awful he was to her, how he pressured her relentlessly for sex ... it's got to be 1 star.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6224558676855142865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2461237131" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8149802707152316250"><strong>Julia Quinn has ruined me.</strong><br/><br/>I am floating, and I don’t want to be disturbed. This blissful feeling is what Julia Quinn makes me feel with each book that I finish. Benedict and Sophie were absolutely perfect. Sophie, Being below his station didn’t stop Benedict from knowing exactly what he wanted. An obsession/love sickness that started over two years ago at a masquerade ball, left Benedict completely “love stoned.” Sophie, being there on the downlow because she was a servant and all, added such a </span>
  <span id="freeText8149802707152316250" style="display:none"><strong>Julia Quinn has ruined me.</strong><br /><br />I am floating, and I don’t want to be disturbed. This blissful feeling is what Julia Quinn makes me feel with each book that I finish. Benedict and Sophie were absolutely perfect. Sophie, Being below his station didn’t stop Benedict from knowing exactly what he wanted. An obsession/love sickness that started over two years ago at a masquerade ball, left Benedict completely “love stoned.” Sophie, being there on the downlow because she was a servant and all, added such a Cinderella type feel to the story, but only 10x better. Circumstances land them together two years later under dangerous and much unpleasantness , but really turned out to be salvation and fate. I can’t even describe or express my intense feelings over this story, just know that I’m forever hooked on The Bridgertons, and I feel Julia Quinn is a genius. I can’t wait for the Netflix adaptation that will air next year. My heart is truly fluttering with excitement!<br /><br />“It was strange, to find a woman who could make him happy just with her mere presence. He didn’t even have to see her, or hear her voice, or even smell her scent. He just had to know that she was there. If that wasn’t love, he didn’t know what was.” <br /><br />Oh, it was very much love indeed.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1315567539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7339146277526929466"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435175037ra/15313538.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>This is magic in it's true form, and it's the main reason why people read.</b> <br/><br/>I know that many of my friends here on Goodreads don't like stories where the hero and heroine fall in love at first sight, but when I read a story like this one, I can say exactly why I love this theme. <br/><br/>It just has to be done in the most realistic way, and only very few authors capture a realistic angle. But Julia Quinn? Wow. <br/>Not only do I believe the love at first sight between Sophie and Benedict from Moment Nr. 1 on, </span>
  <span id="freeText7339146277526929466" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435175037ra/15313538.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This is magic in it's true form, and it's the main reason why people read.</b> <br><br>I know that many of my friends here on Goodreads don't like stories where the hero and heroine fall in love at first sight, but when I read a story like this one, I can say exactly why I love this theme. <br><br>It just has to be done in the most realistic way, and only very few authors capture a realistic angle. But Julia Quinn? Wow. <br>Not only do I believe the love at first sight between Sophie and Benedict from Moment Nr. 1 on, but there is just the right amount of a magic feeling that makes it a delight to read. <br><br>Obviously we have a take on the Cinderella fairytale, and the author did a perfect job. We have everything essential to the original story, but added to it two realistic, human main characters and authentic side characters (not to mention that the side characters are mostly all the other Bridgertons, who are all adorable in their own way).<br><br>Sophie and Benedict are my favourite couple so far, and although this is only the third in the series that I've read, I must warn the other Bridgertons that once I find my faves, I don't let them go easily. <br>Truly, Benedict couldn't have been more adorable. He's not only deeply caring, affectionate, funny in a laid-back way and highly emotional, he's so much more. The perfect Prince Charming without being anything resembling boring.<br>Sophie was the perfect heroine, and I sympathized with her and admired her strength and her beliefs in her principles. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435175037ra/15313539.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435175037ra/15313540.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story was enticing, cute, adorable, and all in all everything a romance should be. Even Sophie's hidden identity kept me awake at night, despite the fact that the plot is well-known.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70251276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6535117764866608586"> <i>On one faithful night Benedict Bridgerton fell in love with a masked woman in silver at no less then at a masquerade ball. She took his breathe away, and stole his heart when the clock stuck midnight and she ran away never to been seen again by him. Even with two years passing he somehow always held out hope he could find her again and feel that strong emotion she ignited in him that night, but when she comes across a helpless maid in need of help, he can’t help but feel he knows her from somew</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6535117764866608586" style="display:none"> <i>On one faithful night Benedict Bridgerton fell in love with a masked woman in silver at no less then at a masquerade ball. She took his breathe away, and stole his heart when the clock stuck midnight and she ran away never to been seen again by him. Even with two years passing he somehow always held out hope he could find her again and feel that strong emotion she ignited in him that night, but when she comes across a helpless maid in need of help, he can’t help but feel he knows her from somewhere before…<br /> Sophie Beckett is the daughter of an earl and a courtesan, due to her stepmother’s hate for her, made her work as a maid, until one night where she could live as a true Cinderella and meet her own prince charming, but things wouldn’t last, now two years after leaving her stepmother’s home she comes across her prince charming once again who doesn’t realize who she is.<br /> Sophie and Benedict have to overcome a large gap in social status and revealing truths in order to reach their happy ever after..</i><br /><br /> <br /> An Offer From a Gentleman had a darker tone then other JQ books, with not a lot of laughs or wisecracks that usually a trademark of her works, but still is able to send a deep message across, that had me reading this book non-stop. <br /><br /> Benedict was trying to find himself, being a middle child out of a famous family; he found it a headache, mostly dishearting to always be called Second or The Second Bridgerton. Trying to break the mold those of the ton have placed him in. Throughout the book you see Benedict flourishes, becoming and finding himself. He was charming and sometimes heartbreaking, it torn at my heart as he deals with his feelings toward Sophie and his masked lady in silver. <br /> Sophia was a strong lead, as she stuck to her guns and her beliefs, never breaking under pressure with her stepmother’s treatment and the facts of her birth. <br /> The love between the two were so heartbreaking sweet and breath taking, (the love scene was sizzling!) as they jump leaps and bounds in order to deal with not only their feelings, but how society at the time would judge them. <br /><br /> While both were great, I felt the true bump in a other wise perfect story was the fact of Benedict forcing the issue of the Sophia, a maid becoming his mistress. Installing her in his mother’s home and then trying throughout to get her into bed. While Sophia kept the truth of her being the masked lady in silver and secret for so long. I felt both were at fault for their actions and as it was dragged out throughout the story, I became frustrated with them for not telling the truth and have more respect. <br /><br /> The golden moments and scenes that brought a few tears to my eyes were the confused feelings Benedict had to face and his words that made you wanna throw your arms around him and hug him with all your might, and a little more about the Bridgerton’s mother Violet who is known to be popular and kind was surprising a wallflower once and how she found love and happiness with her husband. <br /><br /> The Bridgerton sisters were more in the forefront this time around, giving the reader glimpses of themselves with their lighthearted moments. <br /><br /><b>Overall:</b> a deeper and a more serious story, with a look at social class in a time where there were major gaps between peers and servants. Finding one self, breaking the mold and grabbing happiness and love with both hands and finding a fairy tale happy ever after with the one you love. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6535117764866608586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5452821749453218762"><b>Not the Quinn I expected</b><br/><br/><b>Setting / Time / Genre:</b> Regency England<br/><br/><b>Length:</b> 421 pages. <br/><br/><b>Series:</b> You bet.   <span id="freeText5452821749453218762" style="display:none"><b>Not the Quinn I expected</b><br><br><b>Setting / Time / Genre:</b> Regency England<br><br><b>Length:</b> 421 pages. <br><br><b>Series:</b> You bet. And I plan on reading every single one. <br><br><b>Sexy times:</b> A couple. Normal Quinn stuff, nothing earth shattering or anything that should scare you off. <br><br><b>Plan on reading more by the author: </b> Yeppers.<br><br><b>Synopsis in one sentence or slightly more:</b> Heroine is a bastard, there I said it. She's spent the better part of her adult life slaving to her evil step monster and at least one evil step sinister. The other step sister is just confused. Hero thinks she is a maid, hires her, wants her, makes the mistress offer, and things happen. <br><br><b>Heroine:</b> Sophie. She's the best part of this story. Really. You can't beat her down. She will fight, get beaten, stand right back up, and keep on keeping on. At the same time she is loving and lovable. <br><br><b>Hero:</b> Benedict. Meh. He's the meh factor. He is just ok. So, perhaps he is a little less than ok. I mean he's trying to make this awesome person his mistress. This part, I did not like so much. That said, he does rescue her from the clutches of a moron and when it counts, although he waited just a wee bit too long for me, he's there for her. He's no Colin and he's no Anthony. In fact, he's more like the second Bridgerton, after all. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463417307i/19116368.png" width="268" height="188" alt="say that" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Why it did or didn't work for me:</b> This book lacked the Quinniscisms that I so love in all of Julia Quinn's books. Usually, she has me giggling and it all feels safe and it all feels good. This was just so meh. I mean, she had a few snicker moments. Some sarcasm. And some wit. But it just fell a little short. A fun read, just not up to her usual. </span>

<div id="review_2664716188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2664716188" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6972914-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529600203p2/6972914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2664716188?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/6972914-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2664716188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15753816376943898448"><b>
  <i>3.5 STARS</i>
</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547303690i/26906512._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ok... where to begin? I will start by saying that I did end up really liking this story by the end. But, I did have quite of few issues with it along the way. <br/><br/>First of all, it's one thing to create a "Cinderella story" and quite another to practically copy one. In fact, the story was so close to the original that I nearly put it down several times. I only kept going, because I was curious where she would take it, and because I've really enjoyed the series so far and hoped to continu</span>
  <span id="freeText15753816376943898448" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>3.5 STARS</i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547303690i/26906512._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok... where to begin? I will start by saying that I did end up really liking this story by the end. But, I did have quite of few issues with it along the way. <br><br>First of all, it's one thing to create a "Cinderella story" and quite another to practically copy one. In fact, the story was so close to the original that I nearly put it down several times. I only kept going, because I was curious where she would take it, and because I've really enjoyed the series so far and hoped to continue it. So I persevered, and then proceeded to get really pissed off at the spoiled and selfish Benedict, yes our beloved hero and Bridgerton brother No 2, who didn't "grow up" until finally <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[about the 80% mark, where his mother practically had to spell it out for him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> For example, where in Cinderella, do you ever remember the prince saying...<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"I want you to come back to London with me, come back and live with me."<br>She looked at him in surprise.<br>"Be mine," he said, his voice thick and urgent. "Be mine right now. Be mine forever. I'll give you anything you want. All I want in return is you."<br>"You want me to be your mistress," she said flatly.<br>He gave her a confused look, although she couldn't be sure whether that was because her statement was so obvious or because he objected to her choice of words.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Well, I'm here to tell you that that is exactly what he was saying. Yes, I know that times were different, and that he thought she was of a different class. But when it comes right down to it, I thought he treated her pretty shabbily. And the poor thing would take any scrap of affection thrown at her by the lout. I was so happy when she told him no. Although, I thought she could have done it with a little more attitude. <br><br>But, in the end, it all came together, just as I knew it would. The jackass finally got his head out of his ass, and realized what a shit he'd been to her. Thank heavens for happy endings, right? So, now I'm smiling, and ready to move on to book 4!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15753816376943898448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer72010487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16104278279860261818"><i>An Offer From a Gentleman</i> definitely takes its inspiration from Cinderella, but it is still a sweet story with lovable characters written in JQ's own witty style. <br/><br/>Sophie is sweet and spunky. Benedict is a hopeless romantic. Together they make a very charming couple. I loved that Benedict spent three years searching for Sophie after their initial meeting at the masquerade ball. <br/><br/>The confrontation between Benedict's mother, Violet Bridgerton, and Araminta (Sophie's wicked step-mother) when Violet c</span>
  <span id="freeText16104278279860261818" style="display:none"><i>An Offer From a Gentleman</i> definitely takes its inspiration from Cinderella, but it is still a sweet story with lovable characters written in JQ's own witty style. <br /><br />Sophie is sweet and spunky. Benedict is a hopeless romantic. Together they make a very charming couple. I loved that Benedict spent three years searching for Sophie after their initial meeting at the masquerade ball. <br /><br />The confrontation between Benedict's mother, Violet Bridgerton, and Araminta (Sophie's wicked step-mother) when Violet comes to Sophie's rescue is awesome. Most likely my favorite part of the book next to the storybook ending and smart dialogue. Three cheers for justice! <br /><br />A tiny part of me felt sorry for Araminta's youngest (and less-loved) daughter, Posy. She was ridiculed and mocked for being chubby. While she wasn't smart enough to speak up for herself, she was still friendly and warm-hearted at times towards Sophie.<br /><br />I would have enjoyed more humor in this book and more glimpses of the other Bridgerton siblings, but I suppose that's why there are more books in the series. :D Thanks for the recommendation Rane. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16104278279860261818" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25322245-an-offer-from-a-gentleman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=regency">regency</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2531365926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3869848034125745076">3.5 stars. I enjoyed this fairly light retelling of Cinderella. I didn't think this kind of book would be my thing, but I found it a quick and easy read. I liked the MCs and hated the wicked stepmother, as you do. Benedict was wonderful, and Sophie had a quiet personal strength that I liked. I did find it a bit hard to swallow that she didn't leave her stepmother's household when she had the opportunity though. If it was really THAT bad, you just wouldn't have stayed, no matter what.<br/><br/>The magical </span>
  <span id="freeText3869848034125745076" style="display:none">3.5 stars. I enjoyed this fairly light retelling of Cinderella. I didn't think this kind of book would be my thing, but I found it a quick and easy read. I liked the MCs and hated the wicked stepmother, as you do. Benedict was wonderful, and Sophie had a quiet personal strength that I liked. I did find it a bit hard to swallow that she didn't leave her stepmother's household when she had the opportunity though. If it was really THAT bad, you just wouldn't have stayed, no matter what.<br /><br />The magical ball was depicted well, without making the book into a PNR. I also liked that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Sophie did remain illegitimate and yet the author found a way to make it acceptable for them to marry. I was half-anticipating the author crumbling and making her parents actually have a secret marriage so she was really legitimate (as I've read in a couple of other books). I'm glad the author didn't take this easy 'cop-out'. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, a nice addition to the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3869848034125745076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90209186?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>
